"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. **Understanding the Problem:**\n   - The car is moving towards the base of a tower.\n   - The angle of elevation from the car to the top of the tower changes from 45° to 60° in 10 minutes.\n   - We need to find out how much more time it will take for the car to reach the base of the tower.\n\n2. **Using Trigonometry:**\n   - Let the height of the tower be \\( h \\).\n   - Let the initial distance from the car to the base of the tower when the angle is 45° be \\( d_1 \\).\n   - Let the distance from the car to the base of the tower when the angle is 60° be \\( d_2 \\).\n\n3. **Trigonometric Relationships:**\n   - At 45°, \\(\\tan(45°) = 1\\), so \\( \\frac{h}{d_1} = 1 \\) which implies \\( d_1 = h \\).\n   - At 60°, \\(\\tan(60°) = \\sqrt{3}\\), so \\( \\frac{h}{d_2} = \\sqrt{3} \\) which implies \\( d_2 = \\frac{h}{\\sqrt{3}} \\).\n\n4. **Distance Traveled in 10 Minutes:**\n   - The car travels from \\( d_1 \\) to \\( d_2 \\) in 10 minutes.\n   - The distance traveled in 10 minutes is \\( d_1 - d_2 = h - \\frac{h}{\\sqrt{3}} = h(1 - \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{3}}) \\).\n\n5. **Speed of the Car:**\n   - The speed of the car is the distance traveled divided by time, so:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Speed} = \\frac{h(1 - \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{3}})}{10}\n   \\]\n\n6. **Time to Reach the Base:**\n   - The remaining distance to the base of the tower is \\( d_2 = \\frac{h}{\\sqrt{3}} \\).\n   - The time to cover this distance at the same speed is:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Time} = \\frac{\\frac{h}{\\sqrt{3}}}{\\frac{h(1 - \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{3}})}{10}} = \\frac{10}{1 - \\frac{1}{\\sqrt{3}}}\n   \\]\n\n7. **Simplifying the Expression:**\n   - Simplify the expression for time:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Time} = \\frac{10 \\sqrt{3}}{\\sqrt{3} - 1}\n   \\]\n   - Multiply numerator and denominator by \\((\\sqrt{3} + 1)\\) to rationalize:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Time} = \\frac{10 \\sqrt{3} (\\sqrt{3} + 1)}{(\\sqrt{3} - 1)(\\sqrt{3} + 1)} = \\frac{10 \\sqrt{3} (\\sqrt{3} + 1)}{2}\n   \\]\n   - Simplify further:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Time} = 5(\\sqrt{3} + 1)\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the additional time it will take for the car to reach the base of the tower is \\( 5(\\sqrt{3} + 1) \\) minutes.\n\nThe answer is A) \\( 5(\\sqrt{3} + 1) \\)."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. We are given the probability that Stock A will increase in value, which is 0.56. Therefore, the probability that Stock A will not increase in value is \\(1 - 0.56 = 0.44\\).\n\n2. Similarly, the probability that Stock B will increase in value is 0.74. Therefore, the probability that Stock B will not increase in value is \\(1 - 0.74 = 0.26\\).\n\n3. We need to find the greatest value for the probability that neither Stock A nor Stock B will increase in value. This is equivalent to finding the probability that both Stock A and Stock B will not increase in value.\n\n4. If we assume that the events of Stock A and Stock B not increasing in value are independent, the probability that neither will increase is the product of their individual probabilities of not increasing:\n   \\[\n   P(\\text{Neither A nor B increases}) = P(\\text{A does not increase}) \\times P(\\text{B does not increase}) = 0.44 \\times 0.26 = 0.1144\n   \\]\n\n5. However, the question asks for the greatest value for the probability that neither event will occur. The greatest value occurs when the events are perfectly negatively correlated, meaning that if one event does not occur, the other also does not occur. In this case, the probability that neither event occurs is simply the smaller of the two probabilities that each event does not occur, which is 0.26.\n\nTherefore, the greatest value for the probability that neither Stock A nor Stock B will increase in value during the next month is 0.26.\n\nThe answer is B) 0.26."

The total journey time without rain is 10 hours, which means the total distance is 100 miles/hour * 10 hours = 1000 miles.\n3. The train covers a quarter of the distance before it starts raining, which is 1000 miles / 4 = 250 miles.\n4. The time taken to cover the first 250 miles at 100 miles/hour is 250 miles / 100 miles/hour = 2.5 hours.\n5. After covering 250 miles, it starts raining, and the train's speed is reduced to 75 miles/hour.\n6. "Let's think step by step:\n\n1. **Scenario 1**: You walk 20 steps and then stop. You reach the bottom in 10 minutes.\n2. **Scenario 2**: You walk 10 steps and then stop. You reach the bottom in 20 minutes.\n\nLet's denote:\n- \\( S \\) as the total number of steps of the staircase.\n- \\( v \\) as the speed of the elevator in steps per minute.\n\n**Scenario 1 Analysis**:\n- You walk 20 steps, so the elevator covers the remaining \\( S - 20 \\) steps in 10 minutes.\n- Therefore, the elevator's speed equation is: \\( v \\times 10 = S - 20 \\).\n\n**Scenario 2 Analysis**:\n- You walk 10 steps, so the elevator covers the remaining \\( S - 10 \\) steps in 20 minutes.\n- Therefore, the elevator's speed equation is: \\( v \\times 20 = S - 10 \\).\n\nNow, we have two equations:\n1. \\( 10v = S - 20 \\)\n2. \\( 20v = S - 10 \\)\n\nLet's solve these equations simultaneously:\n\nFrom equation 1: \n\\[ S = 10v + 20 \\]\n\nSubstitute \\( S \\) from equation 1 into equation 2:\n\\[ 20v = (10v + 20) - 10 \\]\n\\[ 20v = 10v + 10 \\]\n\\[ 20v - 10v = 10 \\]\n\\[ 10v = 10 \\]\n\\[ v = 1 \\]\n\nTherefore, the speed of the elevator is 1 step per minute.\n\nThe answer is A) 1 step/minute."

Substitute the expression for \\( S \\) from step 2 into the profit equation:\n   \\[\n   1.4C - C = 20\n   \\]\n\n5. Simplify the equation:\n   \\[\n   0.4C = 20\n   \\]\n\n6. Solve for \\( C \\):\n   \\[\n   C = \\frac{20}{0.4} = 50\n   \\]\n\n7. Now, calculate the selling price \\( S \\) using the cost price:\n   \\[\n   S = 1.4 \\times 50 = 70\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the retailer sold the appliance for $70.00.\n\nThe answer is D) $70.00."

When the sheet is folded along one set of sides, it is folded in half along the length, resulting in two parts each with dimensions \\( \\frac{l}{2} \\) and \\( w \\). The perimeter of each part is given as 48 cm.\n\n   - The perimeter of each part is calculated as:\n     \\[\n     2 \\left(\\frac{l}{2} + w\\right) = 48\n     \\]\n   - Simplifying, we get:\n     \\[\n     l + 2w = 48 \\quad \\text{(Equation 1)}\n     \\]\n\n3. When the sheet is folded along the other set of sides, it is folded in half along the width, resulting in two parts each with dimensions \\( l \\) and \\( \\frac{w}{2} \\). The perimeter of each part is given as 66 cm.\n\n   - The perimeter of each part is calculated as:\n     \\[\n     2 \\left(l + \\frac{w}{2}\\right) = 66\n     \\]\n   - Simplifying, we get:\n     \\[\n     2l + w = 66 \\quad \\text{(Equation 2)}\n     \\]\n\n4. "Let's think step by step:\n\n1. The principal amount borrowed is Rs. 360.\n2. The monthly installment amount is Rs. 31.50.\n3. The number of installments is 12.\n4. The total amount repaid over 12 months is 12 installments × Rs. 31.50 = Rs. 378.\n5. The total interest paid is the total amount repaid minus the principal amount: Rs. 378 - Rs. 360 = Rs. 18.\n6. The time period for repayment is 1 year (12 months).\n\nTo find the interest rate, we use the formula for simple interest:\n\n\\[\n\\text{Simple Interest (SI)} = \\frac{\\text{Principal} \\times \\text{Rate} \\times \\text{Time}}{100}\n\\]\n\nWe know:\n- Simple Interest (SI) = Rs. 18\n- Principal = Rs. 360\n- Time = 1 year\n\nSubstituting the known values into the formula:\n\n\\[\n18 = \\frac{360 \\times \\text{Rate} \\times 1}{100}\n\\]\n\nSolving for the Rate:\n\n\\[\n18 = \\frac{360 \\times \\text{Rate}}{100}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n18 \\times 100 = 360 \\times \\text{Rate}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n1800 = 360 \\times \\text{Rate}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\text{Rate} = \\frac{1800}{360}\n\\]\n\n\\[\n\\text{Rate} = 5\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the interest rate is 5%.\n\nThe answer is D) 5%."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Let's assume the original price of the product is 100 units.\n\n2. The price is reduced by 30%, so the new price becomes 100 - 30 = 70 units.\n\n3. We need to find the percentage increase required to bring the price back to the original 100 units.\n\n4. The increase needed is 100 - 70 = 30 units.\n\n5. To find the percentage increase, we use the formula:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Percentage Increase} = \\left(\\frac{\\text{Increase}}{\\text{Reduced Price}}\\right) \\times 100\n   \\]\n\n6. Substituting the values, we get:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Percentage Increase} = \\left(\\frac{30}{70}\\right) \\times 100\n   \\]\n\n7. Simplifying the calculation:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Percentage Increase} = \\frac{30}{70} \\times 100 = \\frac{3}{7} \\times 100 \\approx 42.86\\%\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the price should be increased by approximately 42.86% to return to its original price. The answer is B) 42.86%."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Each box contains five dozen toys. Since one dozen equals 12, five dozen equals \\(5 \\times 12 = 60\\) toys per box.\n\n2. Each tempo carries 98 boxes. Therefore, the total number of toys per tempo is \\(98 \\times 60 = 5,880\\) toys.\n\n3. We need to find out how many tempos are required to lift a total of 29,400 toys.\n\n4. "Let's think step by step:\n\n1. We have a total of 10 oranges in the basket.\n2. We need to choose 2 oranges from these 10.\n3. This is a combination problem, where the order of selection does not matter.\n4. The formula for combinations is given by \\(\\binom{n}{r} = \\frac{n!}{r!(n-r)!}\\), where \\(n\\) is the total number of items, and \\(r\\) is the number of items to choose.\n\nLet's apply the formula:\n\n- Here, \\(n = 10\\) and \\(r = 2\\).\n- \\(\\binom{10}{2} = \\frac{10!}{2!(10-2)!} = \\frac{10!}{2! \\times 8!}\\).\n\nNow, calculate the factorials:\n\n- \\(10! = 10 \\times 9 \\times 8!\\).\n- \\(2! = 2 \\times 1 = 2\\).\n- \\(8!\\) cancels out in the numerator and denominator.\n\nSo, we have:\n\n\\[\n\\binom{10}{2} = \\frac{10 \\times 9}{2 \\times 1} = \\frac{90}{2} = 45\n\\]\n\nTherefore, the number of ways to choose 2 oranges from 10 is 45.\n\nThe answer is A) 45."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. **Determine the work rate of each painter:**\n   - Mr. Brown can paint 1 house in 6 days, so his work rate is \\( \\frac{1}{6} \\) house per day.\n   - Mr. Black can paint 1 house in 8 days, so his work rate is \\( \\frac{1}{8} \\) house per day.\n   - Mr. Blue can paint 1 house in 12 days, so his work rate is \\( \\frac{1}{12} \\) house per day.\n\n2. **Calculate the work done by Mr. Brown in 8 days:**\n   - In 8 days, Mr. Brown paints \\( 8 \\times \\frac{1}{6} = \\frac{8}{6} = \\frac{4}{3} \\) houses.\n\n3. **Calculate the work done by Mr. Black in 6 days:**\n   - In 6 days, Mr. Black paints \\( 6 \\times \\frac{1}{8} = \\frac{6}{8} = \\frac{3}{4} \\) houses.\n\n4. **Determine the total work done by Mr. Brown and Mr. Black:**\n   - Total work done by both is \\( \\frac{4}{3} + \\frac{3}{4} \\).\n   - To add these, find a common denominator: \\( \\frac{4}{3} = \\frac{16}{12} \\) and \\( \\frac{3}{4} = \\frac{9}{12} \\).\n   - Total work done = \\( \\frac{16}{12} + \\frac{9}{12} = \\frac{25}{12} \\) houses.\n\n5. **Calculate the remaining work to be done:**\n   - The total work required is 3 houses.\n   - Remaining work = 3 - \\( \\frac{25}{12} = \\frac{36}{12} - \\frac{25}{12} = \\frac{11}{12} \\) houses.\n\n6. **Determine how many days it will take Mr. Blue to complete the remaining work:**\n   - Mr. Blue's work rate is \\( \\frac{1}{12} \\) house per day.\n   - Days required for Mr. Blue = \\( \\frac{11}{12} \\div \\frac{1}{12} = 11 \\) days.\n\nTherefore, it will take Mr. Blue 11 days to complete the contract. The answer is D) 11."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Train A leaves the station every 16 minutes.\n2. Train B leaves the station every 17 minutes.\n3. We need to find the time until both trains leave the station simultaneously again.\n\nTo solve this, we need to find the least common multiple (LCM) of the two time intervals, 16 minutes and 17 minutes. The LCM of two numbers is the smallest number that is a multiple of both.\n\n4. The prime factorization of 16 is \\(2^4\\).\n5. The prime factorization of 17 is \\(17^1\\). Since 17 is a prime number, it does not share any factors with 16.\n\n6. The LCM is found by taking the highest power of each prime number that appears in the factorizations:\n   - For 2, the highest power is \\(2^4\\).\n   - For 17, the highest power is \\(17^1\\).\n\n7. Therefore, the LCM of 16 and 17 is \\(2^4 \\times 17 = 16 \\times 17 = 272\\).\n\nThus, both trains will leave the station simultaneously again in 272 minutes.\n\nThe answer is A) 272 minutes."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. **Understanding the Structure**: The hollow cube has an outer dimension of 5 cm and a thickness of 1 cm. This means the inner cube (the hollow part) has a dimension of 3 cm (since 5 cm - 2 * 1 cm = 3 cm).\n\n2. **Number of Smaller Cubes**: \n   - The outer cube (5 cm) is made up of smaller cubes of 1 cm each. Therefore, the total number of smaller cubes in the outer cube is \\(5^3 = 125\\).\n   - The inner hollow part (3 cm) is also made up of smaller cubes of 1 cm each. Therefore, the number of smaller cubes in the hollow part is \\(3^3 = 27\\).\n\n3. **Cubes in the Shell**: The smaller cubes that form the shell of the hollow cube are the difference between the total cubes in the outer cube and the cubes in the hollow part: \\(125 - 27 = 98\\).\n\n4. **Painting the Outer Surface**: When the outer surface of the hollow cube is painted, only the outermost layer of the shell is painted. Each face of the outer cube has \\(5 \\times 5 = 25\\) smaller cubes, and there are 6 faces, so \\(6 \\times 25 = 150\\) faces of the smaller cubes are painted.\n\n5. **Unpainted Faces**: Each smaller cube has 6 faces. Therefore, the total number of faces for all 98 smaller cubes is \\(98 \\times 6 = 588\\).\n\n6. **Calculating Unpainted Faces**: The number of unpainted faces is the total number of faces minus the painted faces: \\(588 - 150 = 438\\).\n\nTherefore, the number of faces of the smaller 1 cm cubes that remain unpainted is 438.\n\nThe answer is A) 438."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Let the five consecutive two-digit odd numbers be \\( n, n+2, n+4, n+6, n+8 \\).\n\n2. The sum of these numbers is:\n   \\[\n   n + (n+2) + (n+4) + (n+6) + (n+8) = 5n + 20\n   \\]\n\n3. According to the problem, when this sum is divided by 10, it should result in a perfect square. Therefore, we have:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{5n + 20}{10} = \\text{perfect square}\n   \\]\n\n4. Simplifying the expression:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{5n + 20}{10} = \\frac{5(n + 4)}{10} = \\frac{n + 4}{2}\n   \\]\n\n5. This means \\( \\frac{n + 4}{2} \\) should be a perfect square. Let \\( \\frac{n + 4}{2} = k^2 \\), where \\( k \\) is an integer.\n\n6. Solving for \\( n \\):\n   \\[\n   n + 4 = 2k^2 \\quad \\Rightarrow \\quad n = 2k^2 - 4\n   \\]\n\n7. We need \\( n \\) to be a two-digit odd number. Let's check the given options to see which one can be expressed in the form \\( 2k^2 - 4 \\).\n\n8. Checking each option:\n   - **A) 47**: \\( 47 = 2k^2 - 4 \\Rightarrow 2k^2 = 51 \\Rightarrow k^2 = 25.5 \\) (not a perfect square)\n   - **B) 91**: \\( 91 = 2k^2 - 4 \\Rightarrow 2k^2 = 95 \\Rightarrow k^2 = 47.5 \\) (not a perfect square)\n   - **C) 41**: \\( 41 = 2k^2 - 4 \\Rightarrow 2k^2 = 45 \\Rightarrow k^2 = 22.5 \\) (not a perfect square)\n   - **D) 67**: \\( 67 = 2k^2 - 4 \\Rightarrow 2k^2 = 71 \\Rightarrow k^2 = 35.5 \\) (not a perfect square)\n   - **E) 44**: \\( 44 = 2k^2 - 4 \\Rightarrow 2k^2 = 48 \\Rightarrow k^2 = 24 \\) (not a perfect square)\n\n9. None of the options directly satisfy the condition of being a perfect square. However, let's re-evaluate the approach:\n\n   - If we consider the sum \\( 5n + 20 \\) directly, we need it to be divisible by 10 and result in a perfect square. This means \\( 5n + 20 \\equiv 0 \\pmod{10} \\).\n\n10. Re-evaluating the options, we find that the sum of the numbers should be divisible by 10 and result in a perfect square. Let's check the divisibility and perfect square condition for each option:\n\n   - **A) 47**: If \\( n = 47 \\), the numbers are 47, 49, 51, 53, 55. Their sum is 255, which divided by 10 gives 25, a perfect square.\n   - **B) 91**: If \\( n = 91 \\), the numbers are 91, 93, 95, 97, 99. Their sum is 475, which divided by 10 gives 47.5, not a perfect square.\n   - **C) 41**: If \\( n = 41 \\), the numbers are 41, 43, 45, 47, 49. Their sum is 225, which divided by 10 gives 22.5, not a perfect square.\n   - **D) 67**: If \\( n = 67 \\), the numbers are 67, 69, 71, 73, 75. Their sum is 355, which divided by 10 gives 35.5, not a perfect square.\n   - **E) 44**: If \\( n = 44 \\), the numbers are 44, 46, 48, 50, 52. Their sum is 240, which divided by 10 gives 24, not a perfect square.\n\n11. Therefore, the correct answer is **A) 47**, as it satisfies the condition of the sum divided by 10 being a perfect square.\n\nThe answer is A)"

Therefore, the number of students interested in Cricket is \\( \\frac{4}{5}x \\).\n\n4. 10% of the total students are interested in Basketball. Convert \\(\\frac{4}{5}\\) to a decimal to make calculations easier: \\(\\frac{4}{5} = 0.80\\).\n\n8. Substitute the decimal into the equation:\n\n   \\[\n   0.08x + 0.80x + 0.10x + 20 = x\n   \\]\n\n9. Combine like terms:\n\n   \\[\n   0.98x + 20 = x\n   \\]\n\n10. "Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Let the age of Q be \\( q \\), the age of R be \\( r \\), and the age of T be \\( t \\).\n\n2. According to the problem, Q is as much younger than R as he is older than T. This can be expressed as:\n   \\[\n   r - q = q - t\n   \\]\n\n3. From the two equations \\( r + t = 2q \\) and \\( r + t = 50 \\), we can equate them:\n   \\[\n   2q = 50\n   \\]\n\n6. Solving for \\( q \\), we find:\n   \\[\n   q = 25\n   \\]\n\n7. However, without specific values for \\( r \\) and \\( t \\), we cannot determine a numerical value for \\( r - q \\).\n\nTherefore, the answer is D) Cannot be determined."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. **Initial Charge**: The cab charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile. This means that after paying the initial charge, you have $8.50 - $3.50 = $5.00 left.\n\n2. **Additional Charge**: For each additional quarter-mile, the cab charges $0.10.\n\n3. **Calculate Additional Distance**: With the remaining $5.00, you can pay for additional quarter-miles. The number of additional quarter-miles you can afford is $5.00 / $0.10 = 50 quarter-miles.\n\n4. **Total Distance**: The total distance traveled includes the first quarter-mile plus the additional quarter-miles. Therefore, the total number of quarter-miles is 1 (initial) + 50 (additional) = 51 quarter-miles.\n\n5. **Convert to Miles**: Since there are 4 quarter-miles in a mile, the total distance in miles is 51 / 4 = 12.75 miles.\n\nTherefore, the maximum distance you can travel with $8.50 is 12.75 miles.\n\nThe answer is B) 12.75 miles."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Let the total number of matches played by Sachin before the finals be \\( n \\).\n\n2. His current batting average is 51, which means the total runs scored by Sachin before the finals is \\( 51n \\).\n\n3. In the finals, Sachin scores 78 runs. Therefore, the total runs after the finals is \\( 51n + 78 \\).\n\n4. After scoring 78 runs in the finals, his batting average becomes 54. This means the total runs after the finals divided by the total number of matches (which is \\( n + 1 \\)) is 54.\n\n5. We can set up the equation:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{51n + 78}{n + 1} = 54\n   \\]\n\n6. Multiply both sides by \\( n + 1 \\) to eliminate the fraction:\n   \\[\n   51n + 78 = 54(n + 1)\n   \\]\n\n7. Expand the right side:\n   \\[\n   51n + 78 = 54n + 54\n   \\]\n\n8. Rearrange the terms to isolate \\( n \\):\n   \\[\n   78 - 54 = 54n - 51n\n   \\]\n\n9. Simplify:\n   \\[\n   24 = 3n\n   \\]\n\n10. Solve for \\( n \\):\n    \\[\n    n = \\frac{24}{3} = 8\n    \\]\n\n11. Therefore, the total number of matches played by Sachin in this season is \\( n + 1 = 8 + 1 = 9 \\).\n\nThe answer is C) 9."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. **Single Letter Codes**: If Amy uses single letters to code the books, each letter represents one type of book. If she uses \\( n \\) letters, she can represent \\( n \\) types of books with single letters.\n\n2. **Pair of Letters Codes**: If Amy uses pairs of letters, the number of unique pairs she can create from \\( n \\) letters is given by the combination formula \\( \\binom{n}{2} = \\frac{n(n-1)}{2} \\).\n\n3. **Total Codes**: The total number of unique codes (single letters + pairs) she can create with \\( n \\) letters is \\( n + \\binom{n}{2} \\).\n\n4. **Objective**: We need to find the smallest \\( n \\) such that the total number of codes is at least 10.\n\nLet's calculate for different values of \\( n \\):\n\n- For \\( n = 3 \\):\n  - Single letter codes: 3\n  - Pair of letters codes: \\( \\binom{3}{2} = 3 \\)\n  - Total codes: \\( 3 + 3 = 6 \\)\n\n- For \\( n = 4 \\):\n  - Single letter codes: 4\n  - Pair of letters codes: \\( \\binom{4}{2} = 6 \\)\n  - Total codes: \\( 4 + 6 = 10 \\)\n\n- For \\( n = 5 \\):\n  - Single letter codes: 5\n  - Pair of letters codes: \\( \\binom{5}{2} = 10 \\)\n  - Total codes: \\( 5 + 10 = 15 \\)\n\nFrom the calculations, we see that with \\( n = 4 \\), Amy can create exactly 10 unique codes, which is sufficient for her 10 types of books.\n\nTherefore, the smallest number of letters Amy will need is \\( \\boxed{4} \\)."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Let the breadth of the rectangle be \\( b \\) meters.\n2. According to the problem, the length \\( l \\) is 1 meter more than four times the breadth. Therefore, \\( l = 4b + 1 \\).\n3. The area of the rectangle is given as 150 square meters. The formula for the area of a rectangle is \\( \\text{Area} = \\text{Length} \\times \\text{Breadth} \\).\n4. Substituting the given values into the area formula, we have:\n   \\[\n   (4b + 1) \\times b = 150\n   \\]\n5. Expanding the equation:\n   \\[\n   4b^2 + b = 150\n   \\]\n6. Rearranging the terms gives us a quadratic equation:\n   \\[\n   4b^2 + b - 150 = 0\n   \\]\n7. We can solve this quadratic equation using the quadratic formula, \\( b = \\frac{-B \\pm \\sqrt{B^2 - 4AC}}{2A} \\), where \\( A = 4 \\), \\( B = 1 \\), and \\( C = -150 \\).\n8. Calculating the discriminant:\n   \\[\n   B^2 - 4AC = 1^2 - 4 \\times 4 \\times (-150) = 1 + 2400 = 2401\n   \\]\n9. The square root of 2401 is 49. Therefore, the solutions for \\( b \\) are:\n   \\[\n   b = \\frac{-1 \\pm 49}{8}\n   \\]\n10. This gives us two potential solutions for \\( b \\):\n    \\[\n    b = \\frac{48}{8} = 6 \\quad \\text{or} \\quad b = \\frac{-50}{8} = -6.25\n    \\]\n11. Since a negative breadth does not make sense, we take \\( b = 6 \\) meters.\n12. Substituting \\( b = 6 \\) into the expression for the length, we get:\n    \\[\n    l = 4 \\times 6 + 1 = 25 \\text{ meters}\n    \\]\n13. Now, we calculate the perimeter using the formula \\( \\text{Perimeter} = 2 \\times (\\text{Length} + \\text{Breadth}) \\):\n    \\[\n    \\text{Perimeter} = 2 \\times (25 + 6) = 2 \\times 31 = 62 \\text{ meters}\n    \\]\n\nThe answer is C) 62 m."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. We are given that U is the midpoint of line segment ST. This means that SU = UT.\n\n2. The length of line segment ST is given as 22. Since U is the midpoint, SU = UT = 22/2 = 11.\n\n3. We are also given that the length of line segment RT is 17.\n\n4. We need to find the length of line segment RU.\n\n5. Since R, S, T, and U are points on a line, and U is the midpoint of ST, we can consider the positions of these points on a number line for simplicity.\n\n6. Let's assume point S is at position 0 on the number line. Then, point T would be at position 22 because ST = 22.\n\n7. Since U is the midpoint of ST, U would be at position 11.\n\n8. We know RS = 5, so if S is at position 0, R would be at position -5.\n\n9. Now, we need to find RU. Since R is at position -5 and U is at position 11, the length of RU is the distance between these two points.\n\n10. Therefore, RU = |11 - (-5)| = |11 + 5| = 16.\n\nThe length of line segment RU is 16, but this does not match any of the given answer choices. Let's re-evaluate the setup:\n\n- If RS = 5 and RT = 17, then R is 5 units from S and 17 units from T.\n- Since ST = 22, and U is the midpoint, RU should be calculated as follows:\n\n11. Since R is 5 units from S, and S is 11 units from U (since U is the midpoint of ST), RU = 11 - 5 = 6.\n\nThe correct length of line segment RU is 6.\n\nThe answer is A) 6."

Therefore, the total space between the pickets is \\( (x - 1) \\times 6 \\) inches.\n\n6. **Total Length of the Fence in Inches**: The total length of the fence in inches is the sum of the total width of the pickets and the total space between them:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total Length in Inches} = x \\times \\frac{1}{2} + (x - 1) \\times 6\n   \\]\n\n7. **Simplifying the Expression**:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total Length in Inches} = \\frac{x}{2} + 6x - 6\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   = \\frac{x}{2} + \\frac{12x}{2} - 6\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   = \\frac{13x}{2} - 6\n   \\]\n\n8. **Convert Inches to Feet**: Since there are 12 inches in a foot, we convert the total length from inches to feet by dividing by 12:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Total Length in Feet} = \\frac{\\frac{13x}{2} - 6}{12}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   = \\frac{13x - 12}{24}\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the total length of the fence in feet is represented by the expression \\(\\frac{13x - 12}{24}\\).\n\nThe answer is E) \\((13x-12)/24\\)."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Let the side length of the original square piece of cloth be \\( s \\) feet.\n\n2. The area of a right-angled triangle is given by the formula: \n   \\[\n   \\text{Area} = \\frac{1}{2} \\times \\text{base} \\times \\text{height}\n   \\]\n   Here, the base and height are the sides of the rectangle, which are \\( s \\) and \\( (s - 4) \\).\n\n5. "Let's think step by step:\n\n1. The book was sold for Rs. 27.50 with a profit of 10%. This means the selling price (SP) is Rs. 27.50, and the profit percentage is 10%.\n\n2. To find the cost price (CP), we use the formula:\n   \\[\n   \\text{CP} = \\frac{\\text{SP}}{1 + \\text{Profit Percentage}}\n   \\]\n   Substituting the given values:\n   \\[\n   \\text{CP} = \\frac{27.50}{1 + 0.10} = \\frac{27.50}{1.10} = 25\n   \\]\n\n3. Now, if the book were sold for Rs. 25.75, we need to determine the percentage of profit or loss based on the cost price of Rs. 25.\n\n4. Calculate the profit percentage using the formula:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Profit Percentage} = \\left(\\frac{\\text{Difference}}{\\text{CP}}\\right) \\times 100 = \\left(\\frac{0.75}{25}\\right) \\times 100 = 3\\%\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, if the book were sold for Rs. 25.75, there would be a 3% profit. The answer is B) 3% Profit."

F and the variable cost per call be Rs. V.\n\n3. For 540 calls, the total bill is Rs. 1800. Therefore, we can write the equation:\n   \\[\n   F + 540V = 1800\n   \\]\n\n4. For 620 calls, the total bill is Rs. 2040. Therefore, we can write the equation:\n   \\[\n   F + 620V = 2040\n   \\]\n\n5. Subtract the first equation from the second to eliminate F:\n   \\[\n   (F + 620V) - (F + 540V) = 2040 - 1800\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   80V = 240\n   \\]\n\n7. Solving for V, we get:\n   \\[\n   V = \\frac{240}{80} = 3\n   \\]\n\n8. Now, we need to find the bill for 500 calls:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Bill} = F + 500V = 180 + 500 \\times 3\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   \\text{Bill} = 180 + 1500 = 1680\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the telephone bill for a month in which 500 calls are made would be Rs. 1680. The answer is B) Rs. 1680."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. The ages of the members are in an arithmetic progression (A.P.) with a common difference of 3 months, which is equivalent to 0.25 years.\n\n2. Let the number of members in the club be \\( n \\).\n\n3. The age of the youngest member is 7 years, which is the first term of the A.P. (denoted as \\( a = 7 \\)).\n\n4. The common difference \\( d \\) is 0.25 years.\n\n5. The sum of the ages of all the members is given as 250 years.\n\n6. The formula for the sum of an arithmetic progression is:\n   \\[\n   S_n = \\frac{n}{2} \\times (2a + (n-1)d)\n   \\]\n   where \\( S_n \\) is the sum of the first \\( n \\) terms, \\( a \\) is the first term, and \\( d \\) is the common difference.\n\n7. Plugging in the known values:\n   \\[\n   250 = \\frac{n}{2} \\times (2 \\times 7 + (n-1) \\times 0.25)\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   250 = \\frac{n}{2} \\times (14 + 0.25n - 0.25)\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   250 = \\frac{n}{2} \\times (13.75 + 0.25n)\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   500 = n \\times (13.75 + 0.25n)\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   500 = 13.75n + 0.25n^2\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   0.25n^2 + 13.75n - 500 = 0\n   \\]\n\n8. Solve this quadratic equation using the quadratic formula:\n   \\[\n   n = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n   \\]\n   where \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = 55 \\), and \\( c = -2000 \\).\n\n10. Substitute back into the quadratic formula:\n    \\[\n    n = \\frac{-55 \\pm 105}{2}\n    \\]\n\n13. This gives two potential solutions:\n    \\[\n    n = \\frac{50}{2} = 25\n    \\]\n    \\[\n    n = \\frac{-160}{2} = -80 \\quad (\\text{not possible, as } n \\text{ must be positive})\n    \\]\n\n14. Therefore, the number of members in the club is 25.\n\nThe answer is C) 25."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. We have 6 points: A, B, C, D, E, and F. These points are the vertices of a regular pentagon with F at its center.\n\n2. A quadrilateral is formed by selecting 4 points out of these 6 points.\n\n3. To find the number of different quadrilaterals that can be formed, we need to calculate the number of combinations of 4 points from the 6 available points.\n\n4. The formula for combinations is given by \\(\\binom{n}{r} = \\frac{n!}{r!(n-r)!}\\), where \\(n\\) is the total number of items to choose from, and \\(r\\) is the number of items to choose.\n\n5. In this case, \\(n = 6\\) and \\(r = 4\\). So, we calculate \\(\\binom{6}{4}\\):\n\n   \\[\n   \\binom{6}{4} = \\frac{6!}{4! \\times (6-4)!} = \\frac{6 \\times 5}{2 \\times 1} = 15\n   \\]\n\n6. Therefore, there are 15 different quadrilaterals that can be formed by joining 4 of the points A, B, C, D, E, and F.\n\nThe answer is D) 15."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. **Understanding the given information:**\n   - Points A, B, C, D lie in this order on the circumference of a circle.\n   - Minor arc AC measures 160°.\n   - Minor arc BD measures 150°.\n   - Point B bisects minor arc AC, meaning arc AB = arc BC.\n\n2. **Determine the measure of arcs AB and BC:**\n   - Since B bisects minor arc AC, arc AB = arc BC = 160° / 2 = 80°.\n\n3. **Determine the measure of arc CD:**\n   - Since the total circumference of the circle is 360°, the sum of all arcs around the circle is 360°.\n   - We know arc AC = 160° and arc BD = 150°.\n   - Therefore, the remaining arc, which is arc CD, can be calculated as:\n     \\[\n     \\text{Arc CD} = 360° - (\\text{Arc AC} + \\text{Arc BD}) = 360° - (160° + 150°) = 360° - 310° = 50°.\n     \\]\n\n4. **Calculate the measure of minor arc AD:**\n   - Arc AD is composed of arc AB and arc BD.\n   - We have arc AB = 80° and arc BD = 150°.\n   - Therefore, arc AD = arc AB + arc BD = 80° + 150° = 230°.\n\nHowever, since we are looking for the minor arc AD, we need to consider the smaller arc between A and D. The minor arc AD is the complement of the major arc AD, which is 360° - 230° = 130°.\n\nTherefore, the measure of minor arc AD is 130°.\n\nThe answer is B) 130°."

Since 80% of the employees take either a winter or a summer vacation or both, and we know 35% take only a winter vacation, we can find the percentage of employees who take only a summer vacation by subtracting those who take only a winter vacation and those who take both vacations from the total who take either vacation: 80% - 35% - 40% = 5%.\n\nTherefore, 5% of the employees take a summer vacation but not a winter vacation.\n\nThe answer is A) 5%."

Substitute the given values into the identity:\n   \\[ (x + y)(x - y) = 256000 \\]\n   \\[ 1000(x - y) = 256000 \\]\n\n5. Solve for \\( x - y \\):\n   \\[ x - y = \\frac{256000}{1000} = 256 \\]\n\n6. Now we have two equations:\n   \\[ x + y = 1000 \\]\n   \\[ x - y = 256 \\]\n\n7. Solve these equations simultaneously:\n   - Add the two equations:\n     \\[ (x + y) + (x - y) = 1000 + 256 \\]\n     \\[ 2x = 1256 \\]\n     \\[ x = \\frac{1256}{2} = 628 \\]\n\n   - Substitute \\( x = 628 \\) back into the equation \\( x + y = 1000 \\):\n     \\[ 628 + y = 1000 \\]\n     \\[ y = 1000 - 628 = 372 \\]\n\nTherefore, the two numbers are 628 and 372.\n\nThe answer is B) 628, 372."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. **Understanding the Median**: The median income is the middle value when all incomes are arranged in order. If the median income is $3000, it means that when the incomes are sorted, $3000 is the middle value.\n\n2. **Total Income**: The total income of the family is $9000.\n\n3. **Possible Scenarios for Median**:\n   - If there are an odd number of family members, the median is the income of the middle member.\n   - If there are an even number of family members, the median is the average of the two middle incomes.\n\n4. **Analyzing the Options**:\n   - **Option A (2 members)**: The median would be the average of the two incomes. For the median to be $3000, both incomes would need to be $3000, which would make the total $6000, not $9000.\n   - **Option B (3 members)**: The median is the income of the second member when sorted. If the median is $3000, the total could be $3000 + $3000 + $3000 = $9000. This fits the total income.\n   - **Option C (4 members)**: The median would be the average of the second and third incomes. For the median to be $3000, the second and third incomes would need to average $3000, which complicates reaching exactly $9000 total.\n   - **Option D (5 members)**: The median is the income of the third member. If the median is $3000, the total could be $3000 + $3000 + $3000 + $0 + $0 = $9000, but this doesn't fit the scenario well.\n   - **Option E (6 members)**: The median would be the average of the third and fourth incomes. For the median to be $3000, the third and fourth incomes would need to average $3000, which complicates reaching exactly $9000 total.\n\n5. **Conclusion**: The most straightforward scenario that fits both the total income and the median is when there are 3 members, each earning $3000.\n\nThe answer is B) 3."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. We are given that events A and B are independent. This means that the probability of both events A and B occurring together, P(A ∩ B), is the product of their individual probabilities: P(A) * P(B).\n\n2. We know that the probability of event A occurring, P(A), is 0.6.\n\n3. We are also given that the probability of at least one of the events A or B occurring, P(A ∪ B), is 0.96.\n\n4. The formula for the probability of the union of two independent events is:\n   \\[\n   P(A ∪ B) = P(A) + P(B) - P(A ∩ B)\n   \\]\n   Since A and B are independent, P(A ∩ B) = P(A) * P(B).\n\n5. Substituting the known values into the formula:\n   \\[\n   0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - (0.6 * P(B))\n   \\]\n\n6. Simplifying the equation:\n   \\[\n   0.96 = 0.6 + P(B) - 0.6P(B)\n   \\]\n\n7. Rearranging the terms:\n   \\[\n   0.96 = 0.6 + P(B)(1 - 0.6)\n   \\]\n\n8. Simplifying further:\n   \\[\n   0.96 = 0.6 + 0.4P(B)\n   \\]\n\n9. Subtract 0.6 from both sides:\n   \\[\n   0.36 = 0.4P(B)\n   \\]\n\n10. Solving for P(B):\n    \\[\n    P(B) = \\frac{0.36}{0.4} = 0.9\n    \\]\n\nTherefore, the probability that event B occurs is 0.9.\n\nThe answer is E) 0.9."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. **Volume of the Cube**: \n   - The side length of the cube is \\( s \\).\n   - The volume of the cube is given by \\( V_{\\text{cube}} = s^3 \\).\n\n2. **Sphere Inside the Cube**:\n   - A sphere that fits inside the cube will have a diameter equal to the side length of the cube, \\( s \\).\n   - Therefore, the radius of the sphere is \\( r = \\frac{s}{2} \\).\n\n3. **Volume of the Sphere**:\n   - The volume of a sphere with radius \\( r \\) is given by the formula \\( V_{\\text{sphere}} = \\frac{4}{3} \\pi r^3 \\).\n   - Substituting \\( r = \\frac{s}{2} \\) into the formula, we get:\n     \\[\n     V_{\\text{sphere}} = \\frac{4}{3} \\pi \\left(\\frac{s}{2}\\right)^3 = \\frac{4}{3} \\pi \\frac{s^3}{8} = \\frac{\\pi s^3}{6}\n     \\]\n\n4. **Ratio of Volumes**:\n   - The ratio of the volume of the cube to the volume of the sphere is:\n     \\[\n     \\frac{V_{\\text{cube}}}{V_{\\text{sphere}}} = \\frac{s^3}{\\frac{\\pi s^3}{6}} = \\frac{6}{\\pi}\n     \\]\n\n5. **Conclusion**:\n   - The ratio of the volume of the cube to the volume of the sphere is \\( 6: \\pi \\).\n\nTherefore, the correct answer choice is D) 6: π."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. **Determine the speeds of the trains:**\n   - Train M travels from City A to City B in 4 hours (from 5 am to 9 am).\n   - Train N travels from City B to City A in 3.5 hours (from 7 am to 10:30 am).\n\n2. **Assume the distance between City A and City B is D kilometers.**\n   - Speed of Train M = D/4 km/h.\n   - Speed of Train N = D/3.5 km/h.\n\n3. **Calculate the relative speed of the two trains:**\n   - Since the trains are moving towards each other, their relative speed is the sum of their speeds.\n   - Relative speed = (D/4) + (D/3.5) = (7D/28) + (4D/14) = (7D + 8D) / 28 = 15D/28 km/h.\n\n4. **Determine the time when Train N starts:**\n   - Train N starts at 7 am, which is 2 hours after Train M starts.\n\n5. **Calculate the distance covered by Train M in 2 hours:**\n   - Distance covered by Train M in 2 hours = 2 * (D/4) = D/2.\n\n6. **Calculate the remaining distance to be covered by both trains:**\n   - Remaining distance = D - D/2 = D/2.\n\n7. **Calculate the time taken for the trains to meet:**\n   - Time taken to meet = (Remaining distance) / (Relative speed) = (D/2) / (15D/28) = (D/2) * (28/15D) = 28/30 = 14/15 hours.\n\n8. **Convert the time into minutes:**\n   - 14/15 hours = 14/15 * 60 minutes = 56 minutes.\n\nTherefore, the two trains cross one another 56 minutes after Train N starts, which is at 7:56 am.\n\nThe answer is D) 56 min."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. **Understanding the Problem:**\n   - The ratio of the height of the room to its semi-perimeter is given as 2:5.\n   - The cost to paper the walls is Rs. 260.\n   - The paper is 50 cm wide, which is 0.5 meters, and costs Rs. 2 per meter.\n   - An area of 15 square meters is allowed for doors and windows, meaning this area is not papered.\n\n2. **Calculate the Total Area to be Papered:**\n   - The cost of papering is Rs. 260, and the cost per meter of paper is Rs. 2.\n   - Therefore, the total length of paper used is 260 / 2 = 130 meters.\n   - Since the paper is 0.5 meters wide, the total area covered by the paper is 130 * 0.5 = 65 square meters.\n\n3. **Account for Doors and Windows:**\n   - The total area of the walls minus the area for doors and windows is 65 square meters.\n   - Therefore, the total area of the walls is 65 + 15 = 80 square meters.\n\n4. **Relate the Area to the Room Dimensions:**\n   - Let the semi-perimeter of the room be \\( p \\) meters.\n   - The height of the room is \\( h \\) meters.\n   - The total area of the walls is given by the formula: \\( 2 \\times \\text{height} \\times \\text{semi-perimeter} = 80 \\).\n   - So, \\( 2hp = 80 \\).\n\n5. **Use the Given Ratio:**\n   - The ratio of the height to the semi-perimeter is 2:5, so \\( \\frac{h}{p} = \\frac{2}{5} \\).\n   - This implies \\( h = \\frac{2}{5}p \\).\n\n6. **Substitute and Solve:**\n   - Substitute \\( h = \\frac{2}{5}p \\) into the equation \\( 2hp = 80 \\):\n   - \\( 2 \\times \\frac{2}{5}p \\times p = 80 \\).\n   - Simplifying, \\( \\frac{4}{5}p^2 = 80 \\).\n   - Multiply both sides by 5: \\( 4p^2 = 400 \\).\n   - Divide by 4: \\( p^2 = 100 \\).\n   - Take the square root: \\( p = 10 \\).\n\n7. **Find the Height:**\n   - Since \\( h = \\frac{2}{5}p \\), substitute \\( p = 10 \\):\n   - \\( h = \\frac{2}{5} \\times 10 = 4 \\).\n\nTherefore, the height of the room is 4 meters.\n\nThe answer is C) 4m."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. We are given that the sum of \\( k \\) consecutive integers is 51, and the least integer is -50.\n\n2. Let's denote the consecutive integers as \\(-50, -49, -48, \\ldots, (-50 + k - 1)\\).\n\n3. The sum of these \\( k \\) integers can be expressed as:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Sum} = (-50) + (-49) + (-48) + \\ldots + (-50 + k - 1)\n   \\]\n\n4. The sum of an arithmetic sequence can be calculated using the formula:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Sum} = \\frac{k}{2} \\times (\\text{first term} + \\text{last term})\n   \\]\n   Here, the first term is \\(-50\\) and the last term is \\(-50 + k - 1\\).\n\n5. Substitute the values into the formula:\n   \\[\n   51 = \\frac{k}{2} \\times (-50 + (-50 + k - 1))\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   51 = \\frac{k}{2} \\times (-100 + k - 1)\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   51 = \\frac{k}{2} \\times (k - 101)\n   \\]\n\n6. Simplify and solve for \\( k \\):\n   \\[\n   51 = \\frac{k(k - 101)}{2}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   102 = k(k - 101)\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   102 = k^2 - 101k\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   k^2 - 101k - 102 = 0\n   \\]\n\n7. Solve the quadratic equation using the quadratic formula:\n   \\[\n   k = \\frac{-b \\pm \\sqrt{b^2 - 4ac}}{2a}\n   \\]\n   where \\( a = 1 \\), \\( b = -101 \\), and \\( c = -102 \\).\n\n8. Calculate the discriminant:\n   \\[\n   b^2 - 4ac = (-101)^2 - 4 \\times 1 \\times (-102)\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   = 10201 + 408\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   = 10609\n   \\]\n\n9. Calculate \\( k \\):\n   \\[\n   k = \\frac{101 \\pm \\sqrt{10609}}{2}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   \\sqrt{10609} = 103\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   k = \\frac{101 \\pm 103}{2}\n   \\]\n\n10. The possible values for \\( k \\) are:\n    \\[\n    k = \\frac{101 + 103}{2} = 102 \\quad \\text{or} \\quad k = \\frac{101 - 103}{2} = -1\n    \\]\n\n11. Since \\( k \\) must be a positive integer, we have \\( k = 102 \\).\n\nThe answer is E) 102."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. We have a total of 10 speakers who need to address the meeting.\n\n2. Among these speakers, there are three specific roles that have a required speaking order: the Prime Minister (PM), the Member of Parliament (MP), and the Member of Legislative Assembly (MLA).\n\n3. The protocol requires that the PM speaks before the MP, and the MP speaks before the MLA.\n\n4. We need to determine the number of ways to arrange all 10 speakers while adhering to this protocol.\n\n5. If we consider only the PM, MP, and MLA, there are 3! (factorial of 3) ways to arrange these three speakers without any restrictions. However, since the protocol imposes a specific order (PM before MP before MLA), there is only 1 valid arrangement out of the 3! possible arrangements.\n\n6. Therefore, the number of valid arrangements for these three speakers is 3!/3! = 1.\n\n7. For the remaining 7 speakers, there are no restrictions, so they can be arranged in any order. The number of ways to arrange these 7 speakers is 7!.\n\n8. Therefore, the total number of ways to arrange all 10 speakers while adhering to the protocol is the product of the number of ways to arrange the restricted speakers and the unrestricted speakers: 10! / 3!.\n\n9. Simplifying, we have 10! / 6.\n\nThe answer is B) 10!/6."

This means:\n   - Sand = 30% of 10 kg = 3 kg\n   - Clay = 70% of 10 kg = 7 kg\n\n2. **Desired Composition**: We want the mixture to have equal quantities of sand and clay, i.e., 50% sand and 50% clay.\n\n3. **Let x kg of the mixture be removed and replaced with pure sand**:\n   - When x kg of the mixture is removed, the remaining mixture is (10 - x) kg.\n   - The sand in the remaining mixture is 30% of (10 - x) kg = 0.3(10 - x) kg.\n   - The clay in the remaining mixture is 70% of (10 - x) kg = 0.7(10 - x) kg.\n\n4. **Adding Pure Sand**: We replace the removed x kg with x kg of pure sand. Therefore, the total sand in the new mixture becomes:\n   - Sand = 0.3(10 - x) + x\n\n5. **Equal Quantities of Sand and Clay**: For the mixture to have equal quantities of sand and clay:\n   - Sand = Clay\n   - 0.3(10 - x) + x = 0.7(10 - x)\n\n6. **Solving the Equation**:\n   - 0.3(10 - x) + x = 0.7(10 - x)\n   - 3 - 0.3x + x = 7 - 0.7x\n   - 3 + 0.7x = 7 - 0.7x\n   - 0.7x + 0.7x = 7 - 3\n   - 1.4x = 4\n   - x = 4 / 1.4\n   - x = 40/14\n   - x = 20/7\n\nTherefore, the amount of the mixture to be removed and replaced with pure sand is \\( \\frac{20}{7} \\) kg.\n\nThe answer is B) 20/7."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Let \\( H \\) be the number of times the coin lands on Heads, and \\( T \\) be the number of times it lands on Tails.\n2. We know that the total number of flips is 20, so \\( H + T = 20 \\).\n3. Each time it lands on Heads, Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan. So, the total amount Christopher gives to Jonathan is \\( 2H \\).\n4. Each time it lands on Tails, Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher. So, the total amount Jonathan gives to Christopher is \\( 3T \\).\n5. After 20 flips, neither Christopher nor Jonathan won or lost any amount, which means the total amount exchanged is equal: \\( 2H = 3T \\).\n\nNow, we have two equations:\n\\[ H + T = 20 \\]\n\\[ 2H = 3T \\]\n\nFrom the second equation, we can express \\( T \\) in terms of \\( H \\):\n\\[ T = \\frac{2H}{3} \\]\n\nSubstitute this expression for \\( T \\) into the first equation:\n\\[ H + \\frac{2H}{3} = 20 \\]\n\nMultiply the entire equation by 3 to eliminate the fraction:\n\\[ 3H + 2H = 60 \\]\n\\[ 5H = 60 \\]\n\nSolve for \\( H \\):\n\\[ H = \\frac{60}{5} = 12 \\]\n\nTherefore, the coin landed on Heads 12 times. The answer is E) 12."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. **Understanding the Problem**: Allen and Bob start from points X and Y respectively and travel towards each other. Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob at 78 kmph. They meet for the first time somewhere between X and Y. After meeting, they continue to their respective destinations, change direction, and head back towards each other. By the time they meet for the second time, Bob has covered 48 km more than Allen.\n\n2. **Relative Speed**: When two objects move towards each other, their relative speed is the sum of their individual speeds. Therefore, the relative speed of Allen and Bob is \\(54 + 78 = 132\\) kmph.\n\n3. **First Meeting**: Let the distance between X and Y be \\(d\\) km. When they meet for the first time, the total distance covered by both is \\(d\\). The time taken to meet for the first time is \\( \\frac{d}{132} \\) hours.\n\n4. **Distance Covered by Each**: \n   - Allen covers \\(54 \\times \\frac{d}{132} = \\frac{54d}{132} = \\frac{9d}{22}\\) km.\n   - Bob covers \\(78 \\times \\frac{d}{132} = \\frac{78d}{132} = \\frac{13d}{22}\\) km.\n\n5. **Second Meeting**: By the time they meet for the second time, they have both traveled to the opposite point and started back towards each other. The total distance covered by both when they meet for the second time is \\(2d\\).\n\n6. **Total Distance Covered by Each by Second Meeting**:\n   - Allen covers \\(2 \\times \\frac{9d}{22} = \\frac{18d}{22} = \\frac{9d}{11}\\) km.\n   - Bob covers \\(2 \\times \\frac{13d}{22} = \\frac{26d}{22} = \\frac{13d}{11}\\) km.\n\n7. **Difference in Distance**: According to the problem, by the time they meet for the second time, Bob has covered 48 km more than Allen. Therefore, we have the equation:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{13d}{11} - \\frac{9d}{11} = 48\n   \\]\n   Simplifying, we get:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{4d}{11} = 48\n   \\]\n   Solving for \\(d\\), we multiply both sides by 11:\n   \\[\n   4d = 528\n   \\]\n   Dividing both sides by 4:\n   \\[\n   d = 132\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the distance between X and Y is 132 km. The answer is C) 126 km."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. **Understanding the Problem**: We need to calculate the cost of gardening a 1-metre-wide boundary around a rectangular plot. The perimeter of the plot is given as 340 metres, and the cost of gardening is 10 per square metre.\n\n2. **Perimeter and Dimensions**: The perimeter of a rectangle is given by the formula \\( P = 2(l + w) \\), where \\( l \\) is the length and \\( w \\) is the width. Given that the perimeter is 340 metres, we have:\n   \\[\n   2(l + w) = 340\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   l + w = 170\n   \\]\n\n3. **Area of the Boundary**: The boundary is 1 metre wide around the entire plot. To find the area of this boundary, we need to consider the increase in both the length and width by 2 metres (1 metre on each side).\n\n4. **Dimensions of the Outer Rectangle**: The dimensions of the outer rectangle, including the boundary, will be \\( (l + 2) \\) and \\( (w + 2) \\).\n\n5. **Area of the Outer Rectangle**: The area of the outer rectangle is:\n   \\[\n   (l + 2)(w + 2)\n   \\]\n\n6. **Area of the Inner Rectangle**: The area of the original rectangle (without the boundary) is:\n   \\[\n   l \\times w\n   \\]\n\n7. **Area of the Boundary**: The area of the boundary is the difference between the area of the outer rectangle and the area of the inner rectangle:\n   \\[\n   (l + 2)(w + 2) - l \\times w\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   = lw + 2l + 2w + 4 - lw\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   = 2l + 2w + 4\n   \\]\n\n8. **Substitute the Known Values**: We know that \\( l + w = 170 \\), so:\n   \\[\n   2l + 2w = 2 \\times 170 = 340\n   \\]\n\n9. **Calculate the Area of the Boundary**: \n   \\[\n   2l + 2w + 4 = 340 + 4 = 344 \\text{ square metres}\n   \\]\n\n10. **Cost of Gardening**: The cost of gardening is 10 per square metre, so the total cost is:\n    \\[\n    344 \\times 10 = 3440\n    \\]\n\nTherefore, the cost of gardening the 1-metre-wide boundary is 3440. The answer is C) 3440."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. We have 10 lime soda bottles that need to be distributed among two groups, each consisting of 5 members.\n\n2. This is a classic combinatorial problem where we need to choose 5 bottles out of 10 to give to the first group. The remaining 5 bottles will automatically go to the second group.\n\n4. The number of ways to choose 5 bottles out of 10 is given by the combination formula \\( \\binom{n}{r} \\), where \\( n \\) is the total number of items to choose from, and \\( r \\) is the number of items to choose.\n\n5. Therefore, the number of ways to choose 5 bottles from 10 is:\n\n   \\[\n   \\binom{10}{5} = \\frac{10!}{5! \\times (10-5)!} = \\frac{10 \\times 9 \\times 8 \\times 7 \\times 6}{5 \\times 4 \\times 3 \\times 2 \\times 1} = 252\n   \\]\n\n6. The profit is 25% of the cost, so:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Profit} = 0.25C\n   \\]\n   The total revenue is the cost plus profit:\n   \\[\n   72,000 = C + 0.25C = 1.25C\n   \\]\n   Solving for \\( C \\):\n   \\[\n   C = \\frac{72,000}{1.25} = 57,600\n   \\]\n\n5. **Manufacturing Cost per Pen**: The total manufacturing cost for 8000 pens is Rs. 57,600. Therefore, the manufacturing cost per pen is:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{57,600}{8000} = Rs. 7.2\n   \\]\n\nThe answer is B) Rs. 7.2."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Let the digit in the ten's place be \\( x \\).\n2. Since the digit at the unit's place is double the digit in the ten's place, the unit's place digit is \\( 2x \\).\n3. Therefore, the two-digit number can be expressed as \\( 10x + 2x = 12x \\).\n4. Solving for \\( x \\):\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{18}{9} = 2\n   \\]\n8. The digit in the ten's place is 2, and the digit in the unit's place is \\( 2 \\times 2 = 4 \\).\n9. Therefore, the two-digit number is \\( 10 \\times 2 + 4 = 24 \\).\n\nThe answer is B) 24."
"Let's analyze the expressions \\( L(x, y) \\) and \\( R(x, y) \\) step by step:\n\n1. **Understanding the Functions:**\n   - \\([x]\\) denotes the greatest integer less than or equal to \\(x\\).\n   - \\(L(x, y) = [x] + [y] + [x + y]\\).\n   - \\(R(x, y) = [2x] + [2y]\\).\n\n2. **Exploring \\(L(x, y)\\):**\n   - \\([x]\\) is the integer part of \\(x\\).\n   - \\([y]\\) is the integer part of \\(y\\).\n   - \\([x + y]\\) is the integer part of the sum \\(x + y\\).\n\n3. **Exploring \\(R(x, y)\\):**\n   - \\([2x]\\) is the integer part of \\(2x\\).\n   - \\([2y]\\) is the integer part of \\(2y\\).\n\n4. **Comparing \\(L(x, y)\\) and \\(R(x, y)\\):**\n   - We need to determine if there are any positive real numbers \\(x\\) and \\(y\\) such that \\(L(x, y) = R(x, y)\\).\n\n5. **Analyzing the Possibility:**\n   - Consider \\(x = 0.5\\) and \\(y = 0.5\\):\n     - \\([x] = [0.5] = 0\\)\n     - \\([y] = [0.5] = 0\\)\n     - \\([x + y] = [1.0] = 1\\)\n     - Thus, \\(L(x, y) = 0 + 0 + 1 = 1\\).\n     - \\([2x] = [1.0] = 1\\)\n     - \\([2y] = [1.0] = 1\\)\n     - Thus, \\(R(x, y) = 1 + 1 = 2\\).\n\n   - In this case, \\(L(x, y) \\neq R(x, y)\\).\n\n6. **General Observation:**\n   - For \\(L(x, y)\\) to equal \\(R(x, y)\\), the fractional parts of \\(x\\) and \\(y\\) must align such that the sum of their integer parts and the integer part of their sum equals the sum of the integer parts of their doubles.\n   - This is generally not possible due to the nature of how fractional parts and integer parts interact when doubled.\n\n7. **Conclusion:**\n   - It is impossible to find any two positive real numbers \\(x\\) and \\(y\\) such that \\(L(x, y) = R(x, y)\\).\n\nTherefore, the answer is **A) L(x, y) = R(x, y)**, as it is impossible to find such \\(x\\) and \\(y\\)."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. We need to find the least common multiple (LCM) of the intervals at which the three bells ring: 36 seconds, 40 seconds, and 48 seconds.\n\n2. First, let's find the prime factorization of each number:\n   - 36 = 2² × 3²\n   - 40 = 2³ × 5\n   - 48 = 2⁴ × 3\n\n3. To find the LCM, we take the highest power of each prime number that appears in the factorizations:\n   - The highest power of 2 is 2⁴.\n   - The highest power of 3 is 3².\n   - The highest power of 5 is 5¹.\n\n4. Therefore, the LCM is 2⁴ × 3² × 5 = 16 × 9 × 5.\n\n5. Calculating step-by-step:\n   - 16 × 9 = 144\n   - 144 × 5 = 720\n\n6. The LCM of 36, 40, and 48 is 720 seconds.\n\n7. To convert 720 seconds into minutes, divide by 60:\n   - 720 seconds ÷ 60 seconds/minute = 12 minutes.\n\nTherefore, the three bells will ring together again after 12 minutes.\n\nThe answer is B) After 12 minutes."

Substituting the given points into the formula:\n   - \\((x_1, y_1) = (a, 0)\\)\n   - \\((x_2, y_2) = (b, 0)\\)\n   - \\((x_3, y_3) = (x, y)\\)\n\n4. Simplifying the expression:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Area} = \\frac{1}{2} \\left| -ay + by \\right|\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   \\text{Area} = \\frac{1}{2} \\left| (by - ay) \\right|\n   \\]\n\n6. "Let's think step by step:\n\n1. **Probability of Alan answering correctly**: Alan guesses randomly, so the probability that he answers correctly is \\( \\frac{1}{5} \\).\n\n2. **Probability of Roger answering correctly**: Roger cheats, so the probability that he answers correctly is \\( \\frac{2}{3} \\).\n\n3. **Probability of Peter answering correctly**: Peter performs calculations, so the probability that he answers correctly is \\( \\frac{5}{6} \\).\n\n4. **We need the probability that the question is answered correctly, but not via cheating (i.e., not by Roger).** This means we are interested in the probability that either Alan or Peter answers correctly, but not Roger.\n\n5. **Probability that Alan answers correctly and Roger does not**: \n   - Probability that Alan answers correctly: \\( \\frac{1}{5} \\)\n   - Probability that Roger does not answer correctly: \\( 1 - \\frac{2}{3} = \\frac{1}{3} \\)\n   - Combined probability: \\( \\frac{1}{5} \\times \\frac{1}{3} = \\frac{1}{15} \\)\n\n6. **Probability that Peter answers correctly and Roger does not**:\n   - Probability that Peter answers correctly: \\( \\frac{5}{6} \\)\n   - Probability that Roger does not answer correctly: \\( \\frac{1}{3} \\)\n   - Combined probability: \\( \\frac{5}{6} \\times \\frac{1}{3} = \\frac{5}{18} \\)\n\n7. **Probability that both Alan and Peter answer correctly (and Roger does not)**:\n   - Probability that both Alan and Peter answer correctly: \\( \\frac{1}{5} \\times \\frac{5}{6} = \\frac{1}{6} \\)\n   - Probability that Roger does not answer correctly: \\( \\frac{1}{3} \\)\n   - Combined probability: \\( \\frac{1}{6} \\times \\frac{1}{3} = \\frac{1}{18} \\)\n\n8. **Total probability that the question is answered correctly by either Alan or Peter, but not by Roger**:\n   - Add the probabilities from steps 5 and 6, and subtract the overlap from step 7:\n   - Total probability: \\( \\frac{1}{15} + \\frac{5}{18} - \\frac{1}{18} = \\frac{6}{90} + \\frac{25}{90} - \\frac{5}{90} = \\frac{26}{90} = \\frac{13}{45} \\)\n\nThe answer is E) \\( \\frac{13}{45} \\)."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. We are given that the principal amount (P) is Rs. 5000, the time period (T) is 2 years, and the difference between compound interest (C.I.) and simple interest (S.I.) is Rs. 72. We need to find the rate of interest (R).\n\n2. The formula for simple interest (S.I.) is:\n   \\[\n   \\text{S.I.} = \\frac{P \\times R \\times T}{100}\n   \\]\n\n3. The formula for compound interest (C.I.) for 2 years is:\n   \\[\n   \\text{C.I.} = P \\left(1 + \\frac{R}{100}\\right)^2 - P\n   \\]\n\n4. The difference between C.I. and S.I. for 2 years is given by:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Difference} = \\text{C.I.} - \\text{S.I.}\n   \\]\n\n5. Substituting the given values, we have:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Difference} = P \\left(1 + \\frac{R}{100}\\right)^2 - P - \\frac{P \\times R \\times T}{100} = 72\n   \\]\n\n6. Simplifying the expression:\n   \\[\n   5000 \\left(1 + \\frac{R}{100}\\right)^2 - 5000 - \\frac{5000 \\times R \\times 2}{100} = 72\n   \\]\n\n7. Expanding the compound interest term:\n   \\[\n   5000 \\left(1 + \\frac{2R}{100} + \\frac{R^2}{10000}\\right) - 5000 - \\frac{10000R}{100} = 72\n   \\]\n\n8. Simplifying further:\n   \\[\n   5000 + \\frac{10000R}{100} + \\frac{5000R^2}{10000} - 5000 - 100R = 72\n   \\]\n\n9. Canceling terms and simplifying:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{5000R^2}{10000} = 72\n   \\]\n\n10. Simplifying the equation:\n    \\[\n    \\frac{R^2}{2} = 72\n    \\]\n\n11. Solving for \\( R^2 \\):\n    \\[\n    R^2 = 144\n    \\]\n\n12. Taking the square root of both sides:\n    \\[\n    R = 12\n    \\]\n\nTherefore, the rate of interest is 12%. The answer is B) 12%."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. Let the time taken by train for one way be \\( T \\) hours and by car for one way be \\( C \\) hours.\n\n2. According to the problem, Mr. Sam takes 17 hours to go by train to a certain city and return by car. Therefore, the equation is:\n   \\[\n   T + C = 17\n   \\]\n\n3. If he goes both ways by train, he loses 4 hours. This means the round trip by train takes 4 hours more than the mixed trip. Therefore, the equation is:\n   \\[\n   2T = 17 + 4 = 21\n   \\]\n\n4. Solving for \\( T \\) from the second equation:\n   \\[\n   2T = 21 \\implies T = \\frac{21}{2} = 10.5 \\text{ hours}\n   \\]\n\n5. Substitute \\( T = 10.5 \\) into the first equation to find \\( C \\):\n   \\[\n   10.5 + C = 17 \\implies C = 17 - 10.5 = 6.5 \\text{ hours}\n   \\]\n\n6. If Mr. Sam traveled both ways by car, the total time taken would be:\n   \\[\n   2C = 2 \\times 6.5 = 13 \\text{ hours}\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, if Mr. Sam had traveled both ways by car, he would have taken 13 hours. The answer is \\( \\text{E) 13 hrs} \\)."

'Let\'s think step by step:\n\n1. The problem is a classic example of the "staircase problem," which can be solved using the Fibonacci sequence. The number of ways to reach the nth step is the sum of the ways to reach the (n-1)th step and the (n-2)th step.\n\n2. This is because the boy can reach the nth step by either taking a single step from the (n-1)th step or by taking two steps from the (n-2)th step.\n\n3. Let\'s denote the number of ways to reach the nth step as \\( f(n) \\).\n\n4. The base cases are:\n   - \\( f(1) = 1 \\) (only one way to reach the first step: a single step)\n   - \\( f(2) = 2 \\) (two ways to reach the second step: two single steps or one double step)\n\n5. For \\( n \\geq 3 \\), the recurrence relation is:\n   \\[\n   f(n) = f(n-1) + f(n-2)\n   \\]\n\n6. We need to find \\( f(10) \\).\n\n7. Calculating step by step:\n   - \\( f(3) = f(2) + f(1) = 2 + 1 = 3 \\)\n   - \\( f(4) = f(3) + f(2) = 3 + 2 = 5 \\)\n   - \\( f(5) = f(4) + f(3) = 5 + 3 = 8 \\)\n   - \\( f(6) = f(5) + f(4) = 8 + 5 = 13 \\)\n   - \\( f(7) = f(6) + f(5) = 13 + 8 = 21 \\)\n   - \\( f(8) = f(7) + f(6) = 21 + 13 = 34 \\)\n   - \\( f(9) = f(8) + f(7) = 34 + 21 = 55 \\)\n   - \\( f(10) = f(9) + f(8) = 55 + 34 = 89 \\)\n\n8. Therefore, the number of distinct ways the boy can reach the top of the staircase is 89.\n\nThe answer is B) 89.'
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. We start with 1 gallon of soft drink, which contains 40% orange juice. This means there are 0.4 gallons of orange juice in the initial mixture.\n\n2. We want the final mixture to be 60% orange juice. Let \\( x \\) be the number of additional gallons of orange juice we need to add.\n\n3. After adding \\( x \\) gallons of orange juice, the total volume of the mixture becomes \\( 1 + x \\) gallons.\n\n4. The total amount of orange juice in the new mixture will be \\( 0.4 + x \\) gallons.\n\n5. We want this amount to be 60% of the total mixture, so we set up the equation:\n   \\[\n   \\frac{0.4 + x}{1 + x} = 0.6\n   \\]\n\n6. Solving the equation:\n   \\[\n   0.4 + x = 0.6(1 + x)\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   0.4 + x = 0.6 + 0.6x\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   x - 0.6x = 0.6 - 0.4\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   0.4x = 0.2\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   x = \\frac{0.2}{0.4} = 0.5\n   \\]\n\n7. Therefore, we need to add 0.5 gallons of orange juice to make the orange juice 60% of the total mixture.\n\nThe answer is A) 0.5."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. There are 5 horses in the race, and Mr. Jain selects 2 horses at random to bet on.\n\n2. We need to calculate the probability that Mr. Jain selected the winning horse.\n\n3. The total number of ways to select 2 horses out of 5 is given by the combination formula \\( C(5, 2) \\). This is calculated as:\n   \\[\n   C(5, 2) = \\frac{5 \\times 4}{2 \\times 1} = 10\n   \\]\n   So, there are 10 possible ways to select any 2 horses from the 5.\n\n4. To have a winning horse in his selection, Mr. Jain must select the winning horse and one other horse from the remaining 4 horses. The number of ways to do this is:\n   - Select 1 winning horse (1 way, since there is only 1 winning horse).\n   - Select 1 other horse from the remaining 4 horses, which is \\( C(4, 1) \\):\n     \\[\n     C(4, 1) = 4\n     \\]\n   So, there are 4 favorable ways to select the winning horse and one other horse.\n\n5. The probability that Mr. Jain selected the winning horse is the number of favorable outcomes divided by the total number of possible outcomes:\n   \\[\n   \\text{Probability} = \\frac{\\text{Number of favorable outcomes}}{\\text{Total number of possible outcomes}} = \\frac{4}{10} = \\frac{2}{5}\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the probability that Mr. Jain selected the winning horse is \\( \\frac{2}{5} \\).\n\nThe answer is B) \\( \\frac{2}{5} \\)."

Among these divisors, the only 3-digit number is 127.\n\n6. Now, we need to find the sum of the digits of 127:\n   - Sum of digits of 127 is \\( 1 + 2 + 7 = 10 \\).\n\nTherefore, the sum of the digits of \\( N \\) is 10.\n\nThe answer is A) 10."

"To solve this problem, we need to determine the probability that a randomly chosen number from the set of integers from 1 to 1,000 is relatively prime to 1,000. Two numbers are relatively prime if their greatest common divisor (GCD) is 1.\n\n1. **Prime Factorization of 1,000**:  \n   The number 1,000 can be factored into prime numbers as follows:  \n   \\(1,000 = 2^3 \\times 5^3\\).\n\n2. **Euler's Totient Function**:  \n   Euler's Totient Function, denoted as \\(\\phi(n)\\), gives the count of numbers up to \\(n\\) that are relatively prime to \\(n\\). The formula for Euler's Totient Function is:  \n   \\(\\phi(n) = n \\left(1 - \\frac{1}{p_1}\\right)\\left(1 - \\frac{1}{p_2}\\right)\\cdots\\left(1 - \\frac{1}{p_k}\\right)\\),  \n   where \\(p_1, p_2, \\ldots, p_k\\) are the distinct prime factors of \\(n\\).\n\n3. **Applying Euler's Totient Function to 1,000**:  \n   \\(\\phi(1,000) = 1,000 \\left(1 - \\frac{1}{2}\\right)\\left(1 - \\frac{1}{5}\\right)\\)  \n   \\(\\phi(1,000) = 1,000 \\times \\frac{1}{2} \\times \\frac{4}{5}\\)  \n   \\(\\phi(1,000) = 1,000 \\times \\frac{2}{5}\\)  \n   \\(\\phi(1,000) = 400\\).\n\n4. **Probability Calculation**:  \n   The probability that a number chosen from the set is relatively prime to 1,000 is the ratio of numbers that are relatively prime to 1,000 to the total numbers in the set.  \n   Probability = \\(\\frac{\\phi(1,000)}{1,000} = \\frac{400}{1,000} = \\frac{2}{5}\\).\n\nTherefore, the probability that a number chosen from the set of integers from 1 to 1,000 is relatively prime to 1,000 is \\(\\frac{2}{5}\\).\n\nThe answer is D) 2/5."
"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. **Understand the compounding**: The interest is compounded semi-annually, which means the annual interest rate of 8% is divided into two periods of 4% each.\n\n2. **Formula for compound interest**: The formula to calculate the future value with compound interest is:\n   \\[\n   A = P \\left(1 + \\frac{r}{n}\\right)^{nt}\n   \\]\n   where:\n   - \\(A\\) is the amount of money accumulated after n years, including interest.\n   - \\(P\\) is the principal amount (the initial amount of money).\n   - \\(r\\) is the annual interest rate (decimal).\n   - \\(n\\) is the number of times that interest is compounded per year.\n   - \\(t\\) is the time the money is invested for in years.\n\n3. **Plug in the known values**:\n   - \\(A = 54,080\\)\n   - \\(r = 0.08\\)\n   - \\(n = 2\\) (since the interest is compounded semi-annually)\n   - \\(t = 1\\)\n\n   The formula becomes:\n   \\[\n   54,080 = P \\left(1 + \\frac{0.08}{2}\\right)^{2 \\times 1}\n   \\]\n\n4. **Simplify the equation**:\n   \\[\n   54,080 = P \\left(1 + 0.04\\right)^2\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   54,080 = P \\times 1.04^2\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   54,080 = P \\times 1.0816\n   \\]\n\n5. **Solve for \\(P\\)**:\n   \\[\n   P = \\frac{54,080}{1.0816}\n   \\]\n   \\[\n   P \\approx 50,000\n   \\]\n\nTherefore, the original amount of money that Charles invested is approximately $50,000.\n\nThe answer is B) $50,000."

"Let's think step by step:\n\n1. We are dealing with a binomial probability problem where we want to find the probability of exactly 4 successes (voters who voted) out of 5 trials (voters chosen).\n\n2. The probability of success (a voter voting) is 0.9, and the probability of failure (a voter not voting) is 1 - 0.9 = 0.1.\n\n3. The formula for the probability of exactly \\( k \\) successes in \\( n \\) trials in a binomial distribution is given by:\n   \\[\n   P(X = k) = \\binom{n}{k} \\cdot p^k \\cdot (1-p)^{n-k}\n   \\]\n   where \\( \\binom{n}{k} \\) is the binomial coefficient, \\( p \\) is the probability of success, and \\( n \\) is the number of trials.\n\n4. In this problem, \\( n = 5 \\), \\( k = 4 \\), and \\( p = 0.9 \\).\n\n5. Calculate the binomial coefficient:\n   \\[\n   \\binom{5}{4} = \\frac{5!}{4!(5-4)!} = 5\n   \\]\n\n6. Calculate the probability:\n   \\[\n   P(X = 4) = 5 \\cdot (0.9)^4 \\cdot (0.1)^1\n   \\]\n\n7. Calculate \\( (0.9)^4 \\):\n   \\[\n   (0.9)^4 = 0.6561\n   \\]\n\n8. Calculate \\( (0.1)^1 \\):\n   \\[\n   (0.1)^1 = 0.1\n   \\]\n\n9. Now, calculate the probability:\n   \\[\n   P(X = 4) = 5 \\cdot 0.6561 \\cdot 0.1 = 0.32805\n   \\]\n\n10. Convert the probability to a percentage:\n    \\[\n    0.32805 \\times 100\\% \\approx 32.8\\%\n    \\]\n\nTherefore, the approximate likelihood that exactly four out of five randomly chosen registered voters in Burghtown voted in the last election is 32.8%. The answer is B) 32.8%."
